(July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="font-weight:normal;"><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Germany"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a></span></th><td>2,400<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Languages</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> <br /><a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> (<span style="font-size:85%;">includes <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_language" title="Malaysian language">Malaysian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> standards</span>)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Religion</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Predominantly: <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni</a>)
Sizable minority: <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaivism" title="Shaivism">Shaivite Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vajrayana" title="Vajrayana">Vajrayana Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kejaw%C3%A8n" title="Kejawèn">Kejawèn</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background-color:#b0c4de;">Related ethnic groups</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Other <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">Indonesian ethnic groups</a>: <a href="/wiki/Balinese_people" title="Balinese people">Balinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indo_people" title="Indo people">Indo people</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madurese_people" title="Madurese people">Madurese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sasak_people" title="Sasak people">Sasak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesians" title="Chinese Indonesians">Tionghoa</a></td></tr></tbody></table>
<table role="presentation" class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Nglegena_ha.png/40px-Nglegena_ha.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="19" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Nglegena_ha.png/60px-Nglegena_ha.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Nglegena_ha.png/80px-Nglegena_ha.png 2x" data-file-width="204" data-file-height="99" /></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains letters from the <a href="/wiki/Javanese_script" title="Javanese script">Javanese script</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Multilingual_support#Javanese" title="Help:Multilingual support">rendering support</a>, you may see <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>&#32;instead of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://sites.google.com/site/jawaunicode/download">Javanese characters</a>.</td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Javanese people</b> (<a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a>: Ngoko: <span style="font-size:16px; line-height:2.1em; word-wrap: break-word; font-family:&#39;Tuladha Jejeg&#39;, &#39;Javanese Text&#39;, &#39;Noto Sans Javanese&#39;;">ꦮꦺꦴꦁꦗꦮ</span> (<i>Wong Jawa</i>), Krama: <span style="font-size:16px; line-height:2.1em; word-wrap: break-word; font-family:&#39;Tuladha Jejeg&#39;, &#39;Javanese Text&#39;, &#39;Noto Sans Javanese&#39;;">ꦠꦶꦪꦁꦗꦮꦶ</span> (<i>Tiyang Jawi</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>; <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(both <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_language" title="Malaysian language">Malaysian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>)</span>: <i>Suku Jawa</i> or <i>Orang Jawa</i>) are an <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> native to the <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesian</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>. With approximately 100 million people<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> (as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>), they form the largest <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Indonesia" title="Ethnic groups in Indonesia">ethnic group in Indonesia</a>. They are predominantly located in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">central</a> to <a href="/wiki/East_Java" title="East Java">eastern</a> parts of the island. There are also significant numbers of people of Javanese descent in most <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Indonesia" title="Provinces of Indonesia">provinces of Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.
</p><p>The <b>Javanese</b> ethnic group has many sub-groups, such as the <a href="/wiki/Mataram_Sultanate" title="Mataram Sultanate">Mataram</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cirebonese" class="mw-redirect" title="Cirebonese">Cirebonese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osing_people" title="Osing people">Osing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tenggerese_people" title="Tenggerese people">Tenggerese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samin_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Samin people">Samin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kampung_Naga" title="Kampung Naga">Naganese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banyumasan_people" title="Banyumasan people">Banyumasan</a>, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A majority of the Javanese people identify themselves as <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, with a minority identifying as <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindus</a>. However, Javanese civilization has been influenced by more than a millennium of interactions between the native <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a> <a href="/wiki/Kejawen" class="mw-redirect" title="Kejawen">Kejawen</a> and the Indian <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>—<a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> culture, and this influence is still visible in Javanese history, culture, traditions, and art forms. With a sizeable global population, the Javanese are considered significant as they are the <a href="/wiki/List_of_contemporary_ethnic_groups" title="List of contemporary ethnic groups">fourth largest ethnic group among Muslims</a>, in the world, after the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bengali_Muslims" title="Bengali Muslims">Bengalis</a><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_Muslims" title="Punjabi Muslims">Punjabis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Javanese_historical_texts" title="Javanese historical texts">Javanese historical texts</a>.</div>
<p>Like most Indonesian ethnic groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Java" title="West Java">West Java</a>, the Javanese are of <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian people">Austronesian</a> origins whose ancestors are thought to have originated in <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">Taiwan</a>, and migrated through the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a><sup id="cite_ref-spiller_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiller-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> to reach Java between 1,500BC and 1,000BC.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> However, according to recent genetic study, Javanese together with Sundanese and Balinese has almost equal ratio of <a href="/wiki/Genetic_marker" title="Genetic marker">genetic marker</a> shared between <a href="/wiki/Austronesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Austronesian">Austronesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Austroasiatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Austroasiatic">Austroasiatic</a> heritages.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_Javanese_kingdoms_and_empires">Ancient Javanese kingdoms and empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Ancient Javanese kingdoms and empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg/220px-Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg/330px-Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg/440px-Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="564" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Javanese_Dance_Ramayana_Shinta_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Javanese adapted many aspects of Indian culture, such as the <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a> epic.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a> influences arrived through trade contacts with the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Hindu and Buddhist - traders and visitors, arrived in the 5th century. The Hindu, Buddhist and Javanese faiths blended into a unique local philosophy.<sup id="cite_ref-spiller_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiller-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The cradle of Javanese culture is commonly described as being in <a href="/wiki/Kedu_Plain" title="Kedu Plain">Kedu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kewu_Plain" title="Kewu Plain">Kewu Plain</a> in the fertile slopes of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Merapi" title="Mount Merapi">Mount Merapi</a> as the heart of the <a href="/wiki/Medang_Kingdom" title="Medang Kingdom">Medang i Bhumi Mataram kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The earliest <a href="/wiki/Sanjaya_dynasty" title="Sanjaya dynasty">Sanjaya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sailendra" class="mw-redirect" title="Sailendra">Sailendra</a> dynasties had their power base there.<sup id="cite_ref-survey_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>238–239</span></sup>
</p><p>The centre of Javanese culture and politics was moved towards the eastern part of the island when <a href="/wiki/Mpu_Sindok" title="Mpu Sindok">Mpu Sindok</a> (r. 929-947) moved the capital of the kingdoms eastward to the valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Brantas_River" title="Brantas River">Brantas River</a> in the 10th century CE. The move was most likely caused by the <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_eruption" class="mw-redirect" title="Volcanic eruption">volcanic eruption</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Merapi" title="Mount Merapi">Merapi</a> and/or invasion from <a href="/wiki/Srivijaya" title="Srivijaya">Srivijaya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-survey_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>238–239</span></sup>
</p><p>The major spread of Javanese influence occurred under King <a href="/wiki/Kertanegara_of_Singhasari" title="Kertanegara of Singhasari">Kertanegara of Singhasari</a> in the late 13th century. The expansionist king launched several major expeditions to Madura, Bali in 1284,<sup id="cite_ref-handbook_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handbook-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Borneo<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2013)">when?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and <a href="/wiki/Pamalayu_expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Pamalayu expedition">most importantly to Sumatra</a> in 1275.<sup id="cite_ref-survey_28-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-survey-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Following the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/Melayu_Kingdom" title="Melayu Kingdom">Melayu Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singhasari" title="Singhasari">Singhasari</a> controlled trade in the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Malacca" title="Strait of Malacca">Strait of Malacca</a>.
</p><p>Singhasari dominance was cut short in 1292 by Kediri's rebellion under <a href="/wiki/Jayakatwang" title="Jayakatwang">Jayakatwang</a>, killing Kertanegara. However, Jayakatwang's reign as king of Java soon ended as he was defeated by Kertanegara's son-in-law, <a href="/wiki/Raden_Wijaya" title="Raden Wijaya">Raden Wijaya</a> with the help of <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Java" title="Mongol invasion of Java">invading Mongol troops</a> in March 1293.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Raden_Wijaya" title="Raden Wijaya">Raden Wijaya</a> would later establish <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahit</a> near the delta of the Brantas River in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Mojokerto" title="Mojokerto">Mojokerto</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Java" title="East Java">East Java</a>. Kertanegara policies were later continued by the <a href="/wiki/Majapahit" title="Majapahit">Majapahits</a> under King <a href="/wiki/Hayam_Wuruk" title="Hayam Wuruk">Hayam Wuruk</a> and his minister <a href="/wiki/Gajah_Mada" title="Gajah Mada">Gajah Mada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-handbook_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handbook-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Various kingdoms of Java were actively involved in the <a href="/wiki/Spice" title="Spice">spice</a> trade in the sea route of the <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a>. Although not major spice producers, these kingdoms were able to stockpile spice by trading for it with <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">rice</a>, of which Java was a major producer.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Majapahit is usually regarded as the greatest of these kingdoms. It was both an agrarian and a maritime power, combining wet-rice cultivation and foreign trade.<sup id="cite_ref-wink_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wink-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The ruin of their capital can be found in <a href="/wiki/Trowulan" title="Trowulan">Trowulan</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Javanese_sultanates">Javanese sultanates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Javanese sultanates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="114" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1205" data-file-height="627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Schildering_voorstellende_de_moord_op_kapitein_Tack_in_Kartasura_TMnr_H-796.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sultan <a href="/wiki/Amangkurat_II_of_Mataram" title="Amangkurat II of Mataram">Amangkurat II of Mataram</a> (upper right) watching warlord <a href="/wiki/Untung_Surapati" title="Untung Surapati">Untung Surapati</a> fighting Captain Tack of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (VOC). ca 1684 AD.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> gained its foothold in port towns on Java's northern coast such as <a href="/wiki/Gresik" class="mw-redirect" title="Gresik">Gresik</a>, Ampel Denta (<a href="/wiki/Surabaya" title="Surabaya">Surabaya</a>), Tuban, Demak and <a href="/wiki/Kudus,_Kudus" class="mw-redirect" title="Kudus, Kudus">Kudus</a>. The spread and proselytising of Islam among the Javanese was traditionally credited to <a href="/wiki/Wali_Sanga" title="Wali Sanga">Wali Songo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Java underwent major changes as <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> spread. Following succession disputes and civil wars, Majapahit power collapsed. After this collapse, its various dependencies and vassals broke free.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Demak" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Demak">Sultanate of Demak</a> became the new strongest power, gaining supremacy among city-states on the northern coast of Java.<sup id="cite_ref-Suma_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suma-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
Aside from its power over Javanese city-states, it also gained overlordship of the ports of <a href="/wiki/Jambi" title="Jambi">Jambi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palembang" title="Palembang">Palembang</a> in eastern Sumatra.<sup id="cite_ref-Suma_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suma-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Demak played a major role in opposing the newly arrived colonial power, the <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a>. Demak twice attacked the Portuguese following their capture of <a href="/wiki/Malacca" title="Malacca">Malacca</a>. They also attacked <a href="/wiki/Luso_Sundanese_padr%C3%A3o" class="mw-redirect" title="Luso Sundanese padrão">the allied forces</a> of the Portuguese and the <a href="/wiki/Sunda_Kingdom" title="Sunda Kingdom">Sunda Kingdom</a>, establishing in the process the <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Banten" class="mw-redirect" title="Sultanate of Banten">Sultanate of Banten</a>.
</p><p>Demak was succeeded by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Pajang" title="Kingdom of Pajang">Kingdom of Pajang</a> and finally the <a href="/wiki/Mataram_Sultanate" title="Mataram Sultanate">Sultanate of Mataram</a>. The centre of power moved from coastal Demak, to Pajang in Blora, and later further inland to Mataram lands in <a href="/wiki/Kotagede" title="Kotagede">Kotagede</a>, near present-day <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta" title="Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a>. The Mataram Sultanate reached its peak of power and influence during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Sultan_Agung_of_Mataram" title="Sultan Agung of Mataram">Sultan Agung Hanyokrokusumo</a> between 1613 and 1645.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_Java">Colonial Java</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Colonial Java">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="489" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_%27Het_veertig-jarig_regeringsjubileum_van_Soesoehoenan_Pakoe_Boewono_X_van_Surakarta_in_de_stoet_lopen_serimpi%27s_mee%27_TMnr_10001563.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Javanese courtly ceremony at Keraton Surakarta in 1932.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1619 the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> established their trading headquarter in <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Batavia</a>. Java slowly fell to the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a>, which would also eventually control most of <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Southeast_Asia" title="Maritime Southeast Asia">Maritime Southeast Asia</a>. The internal intrigue and war of succession, in addition to Dutch interference, caused the Mataram Sultanate to break up into <a href="/wiki/Surakarta_Sunanate" title="Surakarta Sunanate">Surakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta_Sultanate" title="Yogyakarta Sultanate">Yogyakarta</a>. The further separation of the Javanese realm was marked by the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Mangkunegaran" title="Mangkunegaran">Mangkunegaran</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pakualaman" title="Pakualaman">Pakualaman</a> princedom. Although the real political power in those days actually lay with the colonial Dutch, the Javanese kings, in their <a href="/wiki/Keraton" class="mw-redirect" title="Keraton">keratons</a>, still held prestige as the supposed power centre of the Javanese realm, especially in and around Surakarta and Yogyakarta.
</p><p>Dutch rule was briefly interrupted by <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">British</a> rule in the early 19th century. While short, the British administration led by <a href="/wiki/Stamford_Raffles" title="Stamford Raffles">Stamford Raffles</a> was significant, and included the re-discovery of <a href="/wiki/Borobudur" title="Borobudur">Borobudur</a>. Conflict with foreign rule was exemplified by the <a href="/wiki/Java_War" title="Java War">Java War</a> between 1825 and 1830, and the leadership of Prince <a href="/wiki/Diponegoro" title="Diponegoro">Diponegoro</a>.
</p><p>Like the rest of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, Java was captured by the <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Empire of Japan</a> during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. With Japan's defeat, independence was proclaimed in the new <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Indonesia">Republic of Indonesia</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republic_of_Indonesia">Republic of Indonesia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Republic of Indonesia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When the Indonesian independence was proclaimed on 17 August 1945, the last sovereign Javanese monarchies, represented by the Sri Sultan of <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta_Sultanate" title="Yogyakarta Sultanate">Yogyakarta</a>, the Sunanate of <a href="/wiki/Surakarta_Sunanate" title="Surakarta Sunanate">Surakarta</a> and Prince of Mangkunegara declared that they would become part of the Republic of Indonesia.
</p><p>Yogyakarta and Pakualam were later united to form the <a href="/wiki/Special_Region_of_Yogyakarta" title="Special Region of Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta Special Region</a>. The Sri sultan became Governor of Yogyakarta, and the Prince of Pakualaman became vice-governor; both were responsible to the President of Indonesia. The Special Region of Yogyakarta was created after the war of independence ended and formalised on 3 August 1950. Surakarta was later absorbed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a> province.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Javanese_culture" title="Javanese culture">Javanese culture</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Javanese_dance" title="Javanese dance">Javanese dance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanisation" title="Javanisation">Javanisation</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Performance.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wayang_Performance.jpg/220px-Wayang_Performance.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wayang_Performance.jpg/330px-Wayang_Performance.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Wayang_Performance.jpg/440px-Wayang_Performance.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2268" data-file-height="1619" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wayang_Performance.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Javanese cultural expressions, such as <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">wayang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a> are often used to promote the excellence of Javanese culture.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Javanese_culture" title="Javanese culture">Javanese culture</a> is one of the oldest civilisations and has flourished in Indonesia. It has gradually absorbed various elements and influences from other cultures, including native reverence for ancestral and natural spirits, <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> dharmic civilisation, Islamic values, and to a lesser extent, Christianity, Western philosophy and modern ideas. Nevertheless, Javanese culture — especially in the Javanese cultural heartland; those of highly polished aristocratic culture of the <i><a href="/wiki/Keraton" class="mw-redirect" title="Keraton">keratons</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta" title="Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surakarta" title="Surakarta">Surakarta</a> — demonstrates some specific traits, such as particular concern with elegance and refinement (Javanese: <i>alus</i>), subtlety, politeness, courtesy, indirectness, emotional restraint and consciousness to one's social stature. Javanese culture values harmony and social order highly, and abhors direct conflicts and disagreements. These Javanese values are often promoted through Javanese cultural expressions, such as <a href="/wiki/Javanese_dance" title="Javanese dance">Javanese dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">gamelan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayang" title="Wayang">wayang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Batik" title="Batik">batik</a>. It is also reinforced through adherence to Javanese <i>adat</i> (traditional rules) in ceremonies, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Slametan" title="Slametan">Slametan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Satu_Suro" title="Satu Suro">Satu Suro</a></i>, Javanese weddings and <i><a href="/wiki/Naloni_Mitoni" title="Naloni Mitoni">Naloni Mitoni</a></i>.
</p><p>However, the culture of <i>pesisiran</i> of Javanese north coast and in Eastern Java demonstrates some slightly different traits. They tend to be more open to new and foreign ideas, more egalitarian, and less conscious of one's social stature. Some of these northern settlements — such as Demak, Kudus, Tuban, Gresik and Ampel in Surabaya — have become more overtly Islamic, traditionally because these port towns are among the earliest places that Islamic teachings gained foothold in Java.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gamelan_Player_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/220px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/330px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Gamelan_Player_1.JPG/440px-Gamelan_Player_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1134" data-file-height="864" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gamelan_Player_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Gamelan" title="Gamelan">Gamelan</a> is one of Javanese cultural expression that demonstrate refinement.</div></div></div>
<p>Javanese culture is traditionally centred in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Java" title="Central Java">Central Java</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yogyakarta" title="Yogyakarta">Yogyakarta</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Java" title="East Java">East Java</a> provinces of Indonesia. Due to various migrations, it can also be found in other parts of the world, such as <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> (where 15% of the population are of Javanese descent), the broader Indonesian archipelago region,<sup id="cite_ref-srilankan_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-srilankan-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cape_Malay" class="mw-redirect" title="Cape Malay">Cape Malay</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cape_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cape-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and other countries. The migrants bring with them various aspect of Javanese cultures such as Gamelan music, traditional dances<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> and the art of <a href="/wiki/Wayang_kulit" title="Wayang kulit">Wayang kulit</a> shadow play.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The migration of Javanese people westward has created a coastal Javanese culture in West Java distinct from the inland <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_people" title="Sundanese people">Sundanese culture</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese language</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Javanese_script" title="Javanese script">Javanese script</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_(Unicode_block)" title="Javanese (Unicode block)">Javanese (Unicode block)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanacaraka-jawa.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hanacaraka-jawa.svg/220px-Hanacaraka-jawa.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="72" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hanacaraka-jawa.svg/330px-Hanacaraka-jawa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Hanacaraka-jawa.svg/440px-Hanacaraka-jawa.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="180" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hanacaraka-jawa.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Javanese_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="Javanese alphabet">Javanese alphabet</a>.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian</a> family of languages and is closely related to, but distinct from, other <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Indonesia" title="Languages of Indonesia">languages of Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-dict_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dict-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> It is notable for its great number of nearly ubiquitous <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> loans, found especially in literary Javanese.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> This is due to the long history of Hindu and Buddhist influences in Java.
</p><p>Many Javanese in Indonesia are <a href="/wiki/Bilingual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingual">bilingual</a>, being fluent in <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a> (the standardized variant of the <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay language</a>) and Javanese.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In a public poll held <a href="/wiki/Circa" title="Circa">circa</a>-1990, approximately 12% of Javanese used <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>, around 18% used both Javanese and Indonesian, and the rest used Javanese exclusively.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Javanese language was formerly written with a script descended from the <a href="/wiki/Brahmi_script" title="Brahmi script">Brahmi script</a>, natively known as <i>Hanacaraka</i> or <i>Carakan</i>. Upon Indonesian independence it was replaced with a form of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>.
While Javanese was not made an <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Indonesia, it has the status of regional language for communication in the Javanese-majority regions. The language also can be viewed as an ethnic language because it is one of the defining characteristics of the Javanese ethnic identity.<sup id="cite_ref-dict_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dict-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_philosophy">Literature and philosophy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Literature and philosophy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Javanese_literature" title="Javanese literature">Javanese literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Javanese_poetry" title="Javanese poetry">Javanese poetry</a></div>
<p>Javanese intellectuals, writers, poets and men of letters are known for their ability to formulate ideas and creating <a href="/wiki/Idiom" title="Idiom">idioms</a> for high cultural purpose, through stringing words to express a deeper philosophical meanings. Several philosophical idioms sprung from Javanese classical literature, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_historical_texts" title="Javanese historical texts">Javanese historical texts</a> and oral traditions, and have spread into several media and promoted as popular <a href="/wiki/Motto" title="Motto">mottos</a>. For example, <i>"<a href="/wiki/Bhinneka_Tunggal_Ika" title="Bhinneka Tunggal Ika">Bhinneka Tunggal Ika</a>"</i>, used as the national motto of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Indonesia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Indonesia">Republic of Indonesia</a>, <i>"Gemah Ripah Loh Jinawi, Toto Tentrem Kerto Raharjo"</i>, <i>"Jer Basuki Mawa Bea"</i>, <i>"Rawe-Rawe rantas, Malang-Malang putung"</i> and <i>"<a href="/wiki/Tut_Wuri_Handayani" class="mw-redirect" title="Tut Wuri Handayani">Tut Wuri Handayani</a>"</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_structure">Social structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Social structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg/170px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg/255px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg/340px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="700" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Portret_van_een_Javaanse_vorst_of_notabele_met_twee_bedienden_TMnr_60004903.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Javanese <i>priyayi</i> (aristocrat) and servants, <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1865.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">American</a> <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropologist</a> <a href="/wiki/Clifford_Geertz" title="Clifford Geertz">Clifford Geertz</a> divided in the 1960s the Javanese community into three <i>aliran</i> or "streams": <a href="/wiki/Santri" title="Santri">santri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abangan" title="Abangan">abangan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Priyayi" title="Priyayi">priyayi</a>. According to him, the Santri followed an orthodox interpretation <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, the abangan followed a syncretic form of Islam that mixed Hindu and animist elements (often termed <i><a href="/wiki/Kejawen" class="mw-redirect" title="Kejawen">Kejawen</a></i>), and the priyayi were the nobility.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Geertz opinion is often opposed today because he mixed the social groups with belief groups. It was also difficult to apply this social categorisation in classing outsiders, for example other non-<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> Indonesians such as persons of <a href="/wiki/Arab_Indonesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Arab Indonesian">Arab</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Indonesian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Indonesian">Chinese</a> and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">Indian</a> descent.
</p><p>Social stratification is much less rigid in northern coast area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Javanese_people&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Indonesia" title="Religion in Indonesia">Religion in Indonesia</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:300px; background: white;">
